Fortunately, the comrades of our party, adhering to the will of the Prime Minister, were united and suppressed the chaos with one heart and one mind. We were happy to see the disintegration of the warlords, the suppression of the reactionaries, the peaceful unification, and the renewal of the people. We could work together to resist foreign aggression and concentrate on eradicating the communists. At this time of stopping the war and the people looking forward to a well-off life, it is unexpected that Committee Member Deng and others disregarded the facts, picked up rumors, and issued 30 telegrams first, and the comrades did not add to their thinking and echoed them later. What is the difference between helping the Red bandits to show their power and giving the great powers an excuse? In the past, comrades repelled the communists and contained the chaos, and their merits were in the party and the country. Therefore, the government relied on them with important places and assigned them special positions. They should not easily believe in蛊惑 and be fooled. They must know that warlords, politicians, and Red bandits are afraid that the world will be in trouble, and they will do their best to鼓唇弄舌, alienate and provoke. Comrades should expose the treacherous schemes. How can they be puppets, isolate themselves from the Central Government, and glorify themselves in the country? Even if they have any suggestions to the Central Government, they should submit them by telegram according to law and listen to the orders. How can they disregard the country, threaten the Central Government, and destroy unification for the sake of quickness? Those who lose their way will have little help, and those who start well will end badly. The defeat of Yan Feng is not far away. Our association feels the danger and dares not tell you. If you can pull back from the brink, it is still not too late to be a hero. If you go your own way, you will be condemned by thousands of people and bring destruction upon yourself. There is no time for regret. I dare to tell you my heart and ask you to think twice. It is fortunate for Guangdong Province and fortunate for the country.

The Military Law Tribunal Was Formally Established Yesterday Morning 125

Presiding Judge and Others Sworn into Office

The Case of Assassinating Yang Hu is Transferred for Trial

The Shanghai Provisional Military Law Tribunal, jointly organized by the Songhu Garrison Command, the Municipal Government, the Municipal Party Department, and the Jiangsu Higher Court, held a formal establishment ceremony in the auditorium of the Longhua Garrison Headquarters at 10:15 am yesterday. At the same time, the presiding judge and judges were also sworn into office.

Attending Representatives More than 20 representatives from various agencies and reporters from various newspapers went to the Garrison Headquarters to participate in the ceremony yesterday morning, including Tao Baichuan, representative of the Municipal Party Department, Wang Yufen and Lin Tao, representatives of the Public Security Bureau, Luo Jingyou, Chief of the Second Section of the Municipal Government, Ju Zhijing of the Special District Local Court, Shen Xinyi of the Local Court, Zhang Dabiao of the Second Branch of the Jiangsu Higher Court, and Tan Shaoliang of the Public Concession Police Department.

Oath and Training After the meeting, Xu Jinyuan, Chief of Staff of the Garrison Headquarters, presided over the meeting and acted as the oath supervisor, and performed the ceremony. Then, Chen Hanzuo, the presiding judge, and Jiang Huaisu, Huang Daolin, Qian Chengjun, and Dai Yuanchuan, the five judges, took the oath of office. Then, the oath supervisor Xu Jinyuan delivered a training speech, saying briefly that the Provisional Military Law Tribunal was established today, and he was honored to participate in the grand ceremony. This agency was organized according to the order of the Central Government, and its main purpose is to use severe punishments in troubled times, and on the one hand, it adopts a system of collective wisdom to meet the spirit of a country ruled by law. The city is a mixed Chinese and foreign area, and communists and reactionaries are concentrated here, so the establishment of this agency is especially necessary. It is hoped that the presiding judges and judges will work hard and not betray the Central Government's entrustment.

Representative Speeches Then Tao Baichuan, the representative of the Municipal Party Department, delivered a speech, saying briefly that the main responsibility of the Military Law Tribunal is the photography of the establishment of the Provisional Military Law Tribunal (Wang Kai).

Second, there should be no injustice, that is, we must be careful and prudent in the trial of cases, and do not allow any false accusations or unjust cases to occur. Second, there should be no leniency, that is, if the criminals are indeed communists and reactionaries, they should be severely punished and not allowed to be lenient. Then Luo Jingyou, the representative of the Municipal Government, and Gao Dengyu, the Chief of the Military Law Department of the Garrison Headquarters, successively delivered speeches, which were mostly encouraging. At 11 o'clock, the music was played, the ceremony was completed, and the final photo was taken and dispersed.

Cases for Trial According to Chen Hanzuo yesterday, the outline of the organization of the tribunal will be announced in the next few days. In addition to the judges, there will be only five clerks. The candidates have been decided, including Chief Clerk Wu Chengchang, clerks Zhu Jiaxiang, Liu Wenqin, Lin Tao, and Li Jianhu. There are more than ten cases for trial, all of which were transferred by the Garrison Headquarters. The case of plotting to assassinate Yang Hu, the military attache of the National Government, is also among them.

Yang Shuzhuang Arrived in Shanghai Yesterday and Will Return to Fujian 126

There is a Solution to the Financial Problems

Yang Shuzhuang, Minister of the Navy and Chairman of Fujian Province, attended the National Assembly and went to Nanjing from Fujian. Since Yang already has a solution, he is scheduled to return to Fujian in the next two or three days. The Jian Puan, which he took, was also ordered to be moored in Songhou yesterday for departure. At that time, Chen Peikun, the provincial commissioner, will go together.

City Sand and Gravel Industry Suspends Business 128

In Protest Against Taxation in Zhejiang Province

More than 1,000 sand and gravel companies in the city suspended business unanimously the night before yesterday in protest against the Zhejiang Provincial Construction Department's increase in management fees and property fees. The details are as follows:

Reasons for the Suspension On the one hand, the suspension of the sand and gravel industry is to protest against the increase in donations and taxes, and on the other hand, it is to protest against Dachang's contracting of tax collection and monopoly of the sand and gravel industry. Since Dachang contracted the sand and gravel tax collection, it also established an Yitai Company to sell sand and gravel and build large ships for loading and transportation. Therefore, the sand and gravel industry, due to the increase in taxes, has to pay more than one yuan of donation and tax for every ton of sand and gravel sold at two yuan. At the same time, the industry has a contract for the sale, and the price cannot be increased. Since Yitai is organized by Dachang, which contracts the sand and gravel tax, it has an advantage. Seeing that there is no profit to be made, the sand and gravel industry automatically suspended business unanimously the night before yesterday to resist.

Public Association Persuades Yesterday morning, Gong Wushou, a member of the Sand and Gravel Industry Association, reported and went to various places to persuade the resumption of work. After all, this time it was initiated by the industries themselves, and the number of people was too large, so it was not effective. Therefore, the public association encouraged them to maintain order and wait for a solution quietly, so the order yesterday was good.

Impact on Construction Since the sand and gravel suspension of business the night before yesterday, the transporting, barging, and loading have completely stopped. As a result, construction sites have a feeling that there is no goods to do. It is said that the construction industry is discussing solutions at a meeting. At the same time, more than 50,000 workers in the trucking, barging, and transporting industries related to sand and gravel are also panicked by the suspension of business.

Appeal to the Authorities After the suspension of business tide occurred, the Sand and Gravel Industry Association appealed to the Municipal Government, the Municipal Party Department, and the Social Affairs Bureau, requesting them to uphold justice and avoid the expansion of the tide. The original presentation said that the illegal levy of exorbitant taxes has triggered a suspension of business tide, and I humbly request the Ministry, the Government, and the Bureau to uphold justice and stop the collection of such exorbitant taxes, so as to relieve the people's plight and stabilize the business. It is said that Dachang Yitai Company only seeks its own interests, and the Zhejiang Provincial Government Construction Department undertakes the production and sales tax of sand and mud, and cleverly establishes names and illegally levies taxes. I have submitted a request to the Ministry for a clear order to abolish it. Then I received a reply in No. 124, saying that the presentation was received, and I have asked the Zhejiang Provincial Party Department to investigate and verify it before reviewing it. After that, I immediately notified all members to strictly observe order and wait for a solution. Then, according to member Gong Wushou's report, now the two companies, Dachang Yitai, are levying exorbitant taxes again and again, and they are also detaining goods and arresting people and threatening in many ways. The industry cannot bear it anymore, so they automatically suspended business together to make a final resistance and organized a petition group to request a presentation. I immediately sent people to investigate and found it to be true. After many dissuasions, the crowd was angry and unable to stop it, and the exorbitant taxes were obviously illegally levied. The association had no choice but to follow the principle of protecting the industry and business and follow the crowd's request and submit a document to the Ministry, asking them to uphold justice and stop the illegal levy within the Jiangsu Province and ask them to forward it to the Zhejiang Provincial Government to request a clear order to abolish the exorbitant taxes, so as to relieve the people's plight and stabilize the business. Police Department Detective Squad Captures Notorious Bandit Wang Liuni of Xiaoxian County 130

Escorted Back to Headquarters from the French Concession

Wang Liujin, a notorious bandit leader from Xiaoxian County, commanded thousands of followers, possessing a complete arsenal of both long and short firearms as well as hand-held machine guns. He roamed freely and acted arrogantly. Recently, he fell ill and secretly came to Shanghai, using the alias Wang Jingxiang, renting a room on the third floor of Fuxing Inn on East Zilaihuo Street in the French Concession. His movements were secretive, but the long arm of the law reached him. Deng Jingming, the captain of the Police Department's Detective Squad, discovered the bandit's whereabouts. Just as he was about to request an arrest warrant, the Provincial Security Department sent personnel with an official letter to the Police Department requesting the bandit's capture. The original letter was endorsed and handed over to Captain Deng for handling. Deng then dispatched detectives Wang Bin, Xu Pengfei, Yang Fengqi, and others yesterday morning (the 19th), along with Chinese and Western detectives from the French Concession Police, to Fuxing Inn, where they apprehended him. He was taken to the French Concession Police Station for a brief interrogation. Unexpectedly, even as the bandit faced arrest and awaited punishment for his heinous crimes, his fierce demeanor did not diminish in the slightest. He brazenly admitted his banditry to the French police. He then pointed at the detectives, saying, "I am only captured by you today because I am weakened by illness. It is Heaven that has forsaken me! Otherwise, even if there were ten times as many of you, I would not fear you at all, and would annihilate you all before my room!" His haughty manner showed his usual overbearing nature. The police station, based on his confession, handed him over to the detectives to be escorted back. It is reported that the squad has already taken him to Longhua Headquarters for further proceedings.

Gold and Silver Industry of Hanshi Requests Reduction of Business Tax 131

Representatives Come to Shanghai to Negotiate

Sheng Runsheng and Yao Xuge Yupi, representatives of the Hankou Gold and Silver Trade Association stationed in Shanghai, came to Shanghai to negotiate with their counterparts to seek a reduction in business tax, and all agreed to assist. The association's petition to the National Government Executive Yuan (Ministry of Finance and Ministry of Industry) and the Municipal Chamber of Commerce's transfer to the Provincial Department and the Business Tax Bureau is recorded below. The petition states that the tax rate for the gold and silver industry is too high, endangering its survival and making it difficult to bear. It earnestly lists the reasons and implores the Executive Yuan (Ministry) to review the situation, forward it to the Ministry of Finance, and amend the tax to be levied based on the capital of manufactured goods, in order to alleviate the difficulties of businesses and maintain operations. An investigation reveals that the provincial draft for the collection of business tax, previously promulgated by the Provincial Department of Finance, listed the gold and silver jewelry industry as a luxury goods retail business, taxing 0.5% of the business revenue. It was deemed that the listed taxable items were inconsistent with the nature of civil businesses and difficult to bear. A petition was submitted to the Hankou Chamber of Commerce to be forwarded to the provincial (imperial) government for consideration and to change the tax to be levied based on the capital amount. While awaiting approval, the Ministry of Finance approved the provincial business tax rate. The business tax rate for civil businesses was not only not reduced but was instead increased to 1% of the business revenue, exacerbating the situation and causing widespread panic. After repeatedly expressing their grievances, representatives were elected on April 9th and April 25th to petition the imperial government. They should have waited quietly for approval, but they dared not be silent again. As the provincial business tax is about to be levied, the tax rate for civil businesses remains unamended, causing daily anxiety. If it is not approved for implementation, survival will be hopeless.

Page 14

Therefore, they dare not avoid criticism and lay bare their hearts, explaining in detail to the Imperial (Government) the differences in nature and practice between civil businesses and the prohibition of luxury goods sales, as well as the reasons why taxes cannot be levied based on business revenue: (1) Observing the gold and silver ornaments operated by civil businesses superficially, they are indeed a kind of decoration, not daily necessities. However, considering the actual raw materials used, gold and silver are commodities circulating worldwide. People purchase them initially because their quality is beneficial for practical use and can never be changed, and because their price is equivalent to modern currency and can be easily exchanged for silver. The intention is less for ostentation and more for savings. This differs from ordinary consumables that are used up quickly and from ordinary luxury goods that are purely for vanity. This is the first point. (2) Gold and silver jewelry stores have an internal structure divided into manufacturing and retail departments. Raw gold and silver are used as raw materials, made into ornaments by hand, and then sold by the retail department. Therefore, each store has a workshop, and the styles of the products are different. The process is entirely about turning raw gold and silver into finished goods, earning a small amount of labor as profit. This is completely different from ordinary retail stores that purchase ready-made goods from factories and profit from them. This is the second point. (3) Gold and silver are commodities used worldwide, and price fluctuations are determined by international exchange rates. Today, with numerous banks, price fluctuations are well known. Civil businesses sell based on market prices and cannot manipulate prices in the slightest. This is clear. Moreover, in modern fashion, luxury gold and silver jewelry is often avoided, with ordinary society and rural women using it more. Considering their intention to purchase with their hard-earned money, it is purely a form of small-scale savings, which is more valuable than using money for any other purpose. This kind of business that cultivates thrift and savings and hides wealth among the people should be encouraged by the government and should not be considered as having a nature that needs to be prohibited. This is the third point. (4) Gold and silver have never been taxed by customs. Even during the era of the likin tax, there was no item for taxing them. This is because gold and silver are one with currency and do not need to bear tax obligations. The establishment of business tax is originally to compensate for the losses suffered by local areas after the likin tax was abolished. The gold and silver industry has never had likin tax, so in fact, there is no need to plan for any compensation. However, as the government has new regulations for business tax payment, civil businesses are also willing to fulfill their tax obligations. However, taxes must be levied according to the nature and actual situation of civil businesses to be in line with the aim of abolishing likin and not cause them to collapse due to heavy taxes. This is the fourth point. In summary, the gold and silver ornaments operated by civil businesses are not only different in nature from consumables and luxury goods, but also completely different from the situations of prohibiting sales. Moreover, they were previously tax-free items and should be taxed according to the manufacturing industry, based on the capital amount, to be fair and equitable. In recent years, gold prices have soared, and the purchasing power of society is weak. In addition, women are competing to cut their hair short, and fewer people are wearing jewelry. Civil businesses are in a slump and can hardly sustain themselves. They are merely trying to maintain the status quo for the sake of the tens of thousands of workers who depend on them for their livelihoods. Generally misunderstood, they are often regarded as luxury businesses. It is not known that the luxury items among jewelry are not gold and silver but diamonds, pearls, platinum, and jade. These are all products of specialized jewelry stores and foreign jewelry stores, which cannot be compared to civil businesses that focus on gold and silver jewelry. The facts are all there and can be thoroughly investigated. In addition, modern commercial competition is fierce, and profit margins are becoming thinner. The profit margins of civil businesses are no different from those of ordinary commercial businesses, while the cost and monthly interest borne by the goods are higher than those of ordinary goods. If taxes are levied based on business revenue, the taxes borne on the cost of civil business goods will be more than any other goods, and the capital will inevitably be exhausted along with the tax revenue. How can they survive? Thinking of this, they cannot help but shudder. Furthermore, it must be clarified that society often says that gold and silver shops have splendid decorations on the outside and are resplendent inside, and that it is not excessive to impose heavy taxes on them. These superficial words are most likely to confuse the truth. It is not known that paying attention to decoration is a kind of advertising method in business warfare, and it does not seem that splendid and magnificent circumstances can constitute a reason to impose heavy taxes. This is explained in detail to the Ministry. How can the government's tax rate be based on appearances as the standard without examining the nature? This is also the actual situation that civil businesses cannot bear when taxes are levied based on business revenue. In short, civil businesses have always paid taxes and dared not fall behind others. If taxes are levied based on business revenue this time, it is indeed beyond their ability to bear, and it is not that they are not striving to overcome the difficulties. If they can endure the pain and support themselves, they will definitely not appeal repeatedly. They have long admired the Court (Government) for its thorough consideration of the difficulties of businesses. They earnestly implore you to grant a review and approve the transfer to the Ministry of Finance to revise the provincial business tax rate for gold and silver jewelry, taxing it according to the manufacturing industry based on the capital amount, to be in line with the actual situation and maintain survival. They are extremely anxious to await orders. In addition to submitting it separately, it is respectfully submitted to the Executive Yuan, the Ministry of Finance, the Ministry of Industry, the Provincial Department of Finance's Business Tax Bureau, and the Chamber of Commerce for forwarding.

Silk and Cocoon Industry Should Not Be Subjected to Business Tax Again 132

The Municipal Chamber of Commerce Telegraphed to the Ministry of Finance Yesterday, Saying: To the Nanjing Ministry of Finance: On the 18th of this month, we received a letter from the Silk Factory Trade Association of this city stating that Jiang, Zhejiang, and Hubei provinces have recently included the silk and cocoon industry in the scope of business tax collection, which violates the Business Tax Outline and Supplementary Measures. We respectfully request your association to unanimously advocate and support this. An investigation reveals that the business tax regulations proposed by Jiang, Zhejiang, and other provinces list silk and silkworm industries as a type of goods sales industry. When your Ministry reviewed these, these types were retained and not removed. Now, after carefully examining the various points presented by the association, we believe that there are indeed points that can be studied. As the special consumption tax has been explicitly exempted by the National Government, special taxes on silk will also be exempted. It seems that Article 1 of the outline cited in the original letter is no longer applicable. As for why silkworm businesses should not be subject to business tax again, firstly, when silk factories in the interior set up businesses to collect silkworms, they are peasant-like in nature. According to your Ministry's explanation, those who only buy and do not sell and have no business income are naturally exempt from business tax. Secondly, silkworm businesses have always been established with licenses. According to Article 11 of the Supplementary Measures, those who have already paid the brokerage tax, which is now called business tax, will naturally not pay tax again. Therefore, the association's claim that silkworm businesses should not be subject to business tax has a solid legal basis. We respectfully forward this information by telegraph, hoping that your Ministry will review it and instruct to make revisions, which would be a public convenience. Shanghai Chamber of Commerce.

Oil and Sesame Industry Requests Reassessment of Export Tax Rate 133

Telegraph to the Ministry of Finance

The Oil and Sesame Trade Association telegraphed to the Ministry of Finance, saying: To Minister Song of the Ministry of Finance: We respectfully read your Ministry's announcement of the new export tariff, which sets the taxable price of tung oil at 21.099 per picul, with a tax rate of 0.75%, calculated at 1 tael and 6 mace of customs taels. The note states that it is based on the 1929 valuation. After reading it, we were greatly shocked. How can the export of tung oil from our country be based on the price two or three years ago? Exports fluctuate and prices rise and fall. Since the beginning of last spring, exports have decreased from 3,000 to 4,000 tons per month to less than 1,000 tons, and prices have plummeted. As of this spring, the price at the origin is only 15 or 16 taels per picul. The decline in business is evident from this. The reduction in exports can be verified by the export customs statements, which are not just empty words from merchants. The reason for this is that tung oil from our country is sold abroad, with the Americas accounting for 70% to 80%. It is now heard that tung trees are being planted in the United States and have already yielded harvests. Last year, they could produce 1,700 tons, and this year they are expected to produce 15,000 tons. The rapid progress of agricultural products in Europe and America is truly astonishing. This is due to the effects of government promotion and rewards. The export of tung oil from our country has a history of more than ten years. The most prosperous period was between 1928 and 1929. At that time, the gold exchange rate was still low, and the market price was always above 20 taels. If measured by the current gold exchange rate, even 40 or 50 taels would not be excessive. However, now the market price is low and exports have decreased. According to reports, the price in the United States was 12 cents per pound, but it has now fallen to just over 6 cents, with supply exceeding demand in the market. This has a great and significant impact on our country's exports. Merchants, seeing that the export of tung oil is becoming an arrow at the end of its flight, are in a state of bewilderment and do not know what to do. This year, after your Ministry announced the abolition of the likin tax, merchants celebrated the exemption of the harsh tax. The export of tung oil, which was on the verge of extinction, may have a glimmer of hope. They were planning to take advantage of this opportunity to reduce costs and compete with European and American products to regain the position of two or three years ago. Unexpectedly, the taxable price in the new export tariff announced this time is based on the 1929 market price of 21.099, with a heavy tax of 1 tael and 6 mace of customs taels. Using the rare market price of several decades ago as the standard for taxation is going in the opposite direction and putting a square peg in a round hole. Merchants are affected by the promotion of domestic cultivation by foreign countries and are constrained by the heavy new tax rate internally. Export trade is repeatedly hit, and declining industries are pushed into an even more desperate situation. This is contrary to the government's major policies of encouraging industry, promoting domestic goods, and selling abroad. The original export tariff set the taxable price of tung oil at 6 taels per picul, with a tax rate of 5%, calculated at 3 mace of customs taels, plus a 25% surtax of 1 mace and 5 fen, totaling only 4 mace and 5 fen. Now that the surtax has been removed, the regular tax has increased to 1 tael and 6 mace, an increase of about 2.56 times, which is shocking to hear. At a time when European and American countries consider tung oil to be a special product of our country and are competing to plant it themselves in order to resist it, our government should take drastic measures to reduce tax rates and support it, so that the dying industry can have a glimmer of hope for survival. As for the estimation of the taxable price, the cost of production at the origin should be used as the standard. Although it sold for more than 20 taels in 1928 and 1929, it was only for a very short time and in small quantities, so it cannot be used as a standard. According to the current market price at the origin, the price hovers between 15, 16, and 17 taels. However, foreign merchants have announced that if the market price does not return to the 11 or 12 taels of ten years ago, buyers will probably disappear from our country's markets. Although the words are exaggerated, the sudden decrease in export volume is credible. Therefore, if the taxable price must be reassessed, it cannot exceed 10 taels, and the tax rate can only be 5%. Otherwise, it will be resisted externally and burdened by heavy taxes internally. Even if merchants try their best to survive, they will probably be on the verge of extinction. If your Ministry believes that the established tax rate cannot be changed, then what dare merchants do to make suggestions? However, if export trade cannot be developed, not only will the tung oil export business, which has a history of more than ten years, be lost, but also the impact on export tax revenue will not be small. Increasing the tax will result in losses, while reducing it will result in benefits. We hope that your Ministry will choose wisely. We have long admired your Ministry's concern for domestic goods and the promotion of sales abroad. This time, in the revision of the new export tariff, there are many intricate details, and it is difficult to avoid oversights. Merchants' interests are at stake, and the public is in shock. The association deeply knows the crux of the problem and cannot remain silent. It has no choice but to take the liberty of presenting the facts and hopes to be heard. We respectfully implore you, Minister, to consider the difficulties of businesses, quickly revise the export tariff for tung oil to reduce the tax rate, and reassess the taxable price, so that the declining industry can be freed from restrictions and develop and benefit sales. We also request your instructions to be followed. We are extremely anxious to await orders. Respectfully submitted, Shanghai Oil and Sesame Trade Association, May 20, 1931.

Meat Merchants Still Continuing to Suspend Business

The local fresh meat industry has been suspending business for five days due to the slaughter tax issue. The following is a record of the various situations obtained yesterday:

Municipal Bureau of Finance Proclamation: The Municipal Bureau of Finance issued a proclamation yesterday due to the fact that meat merchants throughout the city have not yet opened for business. The proclamation stated: "Regarding the slaughter tax in the city, it was approved by the central government and used exclusively for education funds. It was previously contracted to merchants by the Jiangsu Education Fund Management Office. Now, for the sake of unified governance, it has been transferred to the city for collection. On May 1st, the bureau's various collection offices began selling tax stamps and implementing the collection. A public notice was also issued. The tax rate is 19 cents per pig slaughtered and 20 cents per sheep slaughtered, which is the same as the tax rate when it was contracted to merchants in the past. Tax stamps can also be purchased individually for the convenience of taxpayers. However, there are villains spreading rumors that the tax rate will increase once the slaughter tax is taken back by the government, forcing all meat merchants to go on strike in order to gain leverage and achieve their goals of profiting and enriching themselves. Spreading rumors and deceiving the public is extremely hateful. In addition to reporting this to the Municipal Government and investigating the rumor-mongers for strict punishment according to the law, we hereby issue another proclamation: Meat merchants, many of you are discerning. You must know that the bureau's direct tax collection is to eliminate the evils of monopoly by contractors, to turn private into public, and to conform to the tax system. Since the tax rate is not changed, how can the burden be increased? You should open for business immediately, purchase tax stamps in accordance with the regulations, and not be fooled by others, hesitate to watch, and bring losses to yourselves. This is extremely important. Proclamation."

Bureau of Public Health Advice: To all meat shops: The bureau knows that you have been incited by a few people who want to contract the slaughter tax, blindly following and echoing them, waving the flag and shouting for those with ulterior motives, and even stopping business, becoming the sacrificial victims of those schemers. Because the bureau handles matters such as inspecting livestock, it has close contact with the fresh meat industry and knows very well that you are not making a three-fold profit. It also knows that you are often exploited and manipulated. As long as someone incites you with the good-sounding slogan of "leading you to resist taxes," you will not ask whether the reason is justified or whether the inciter has any secret schemes. You abandon reason as soon as you hear sweet words and obliterate your own opinions as soon as you hear exciting words. This phenomenon is extremely regrettable and pitiful. Therefore, the bureau published a piece of advice in the newspaper (see the local news column of the May 15th Shenbao, Xinwenbao, and Minguo Ribao). It is feared that many meat shops have not seen it or have not understood it even if they have seen it. Therefore, we are now advising you again, hoping that everyone will study it from legal and factual aspects and think about this matter calmly. You must act to maintain your own position and status and have a proper understanding, so that you will not become puppets of others. You must have the courage to accept good advice to be enlightened citizens. Now, we will divide it into several sections for you to think about: (1) The contract tax system cannot avoid the evils of corruption and profit-seeking. It is a termite between public revenue and the burden on businesses. As for the direct collection of taxes based on the quantity of goods by legal tax collection agencies, it is a fair and honest method. Now, the Municipal Government has first abolished the bad system of contracting the slaughter tax and implemented a fair and honest method. You should wholeheartedly support it in good conscience. But you disregard justice, follow those who want to contract and oppose the reform that conforms to reason. What is the reason? (2) Or perhaps some meat shops had colluded with the contractors in the past, privately compromising and reducing the slaughter tax that should have been paid, and sharing the public revenue that should have belonged to the government. Now that the contract system has been broken, they can no longer seek the advantage of sharing the tax that should have been paid. Therefore, they support the opposition. But is this behavior of infringing on public revenue right? Is this sharing behavior legitimate? What is the reason for you to support the opposition to the slaughter tax? (3) The slaughter tax was originally contracted by the Jiangsu Provincial Government to merchants. Now, the Municipal Government of this city has exercised the legal authority to collect taxes in accordance with the central government's resolution. The tax rate for tax collection has not increased. Meat shops are only changing the slaughter tax they should have paid to the Municipal Government. The Municipal Government must also allocate a certain amount to offset the education funds of Jiangsu Province. It is not a newly created tax, nor has it increased your burden. What is the unbreakable reason for blindly following and opposing it, and for going on strike meaninglessly? (4) Someone is inciting and spreading rumors, saying that the Bureau of Finance is now collecting the slaughter tax and requires the purchase of whole books of tax stamps, which is inconvenient for meat merchants. However, according to inquiries made by the bureau, tax stamps, whether whole books or individual sheets, can be taken by meat merchants at their discretion and can be used to pay the slaughter tax anywhere in the city. How could everyone easily believe those inciting rumors? How could it be worth going on strike for this? What is the legitimate reason for supporting the opposition? Based on the above discussion, should the slaughter tax be paid in accordance with the regulations? Thinking about it rationally, there is really no reason to oppose it. People with other agendas also want to bring up legitimate facts such as the city's inspection of livestock and the construction of slaughterhouses to incite everyone and use them as a front for demanding things from the government, which is too sinister and shows too little respect for meat shops, assuming that they are all naive and can be manipulated and exploited at will. Everyone must not be willing to be deceived and fooled in this way. But because the inside story of the deception has not been exposed, everyone has been fooled and does not yet know it. Therefore, everyone should wake up quickly, no longer be fooled, resume business as soon as possible, and avoid losses. If there are people who use violence or threats, you can report them secretly to the authorities and request protection and arrest them separately, or report them to the police officers nearby. The police officers should definitely stop them. The bureau's repeated advice is based entirely on the pursuit of legal principles, deeply considering the pain of meat shops being deceived and coerced, and using sincere advice. It is essential that you accept good words and resume business quickly.

Trade Association Letter: The Fresh Meat Trade Association sent a letter to all sectors yesterday, stating: "Respected sirs, our trade association was ordered by the Jiangsu Department of Finance in 1915 to pay slaughter tax in accordance with the regulations. In 1926, it was collected by the Jiangsu Education Management Office at a tax of 3.9 cents per animal. It has always been contracted by the trade association and only collected from the trade association in the north and south cities. All those in the concessions are not collected. Therefore, compared with the trade association in the concessions, the trade association in the interior has suffered greatly in business. In addition, the areas of Zhabei, Shangbao, and the four rural areas are different from the urban area of Nanshi. The market is depressed. Therefore, the trade association in Zhabei and the four rural areas have always agreed on the amount of tax and paid it monthly, so they have been at peace for more than ten years. Now, the central government, in order to relieve the suffering of the people, has issued orders to abolish likin taxes in various provinces, and all local miscellaneous taxes are exempt. However, slaughter tax is one of the miscellaneous taxes. According to the central government's orders, it should be abolished. Our trade association and others were hoping that the central government would issue a general order to exempt it and reduce the burden. Unexpectedly, the Shanghai Municipal Government has intensified its efforts, forcing all trade associations in the city to buy tickets and collect taxes per animal, which has led to the unanimous opposition of our trade association and others. In order to take care of national taxes and the aftermath of the trade association, our association submitted petitions to the Citizens Training Committee, the Municipal Bureau of Social Affairs, the Municipal Chamber of Commerce, and the various tax rule committees, requesting the Municipal Government to consider the difficulties of businesses and change the municipal slaughter tax to be paid as a national business tax, in line with the principle of one industry, one tax. However, the Municipal Government does not follow public opinion and still uses coercive measures, ordering our trade association and others to buy tickets and pay taxes per animal. Our trade association and others have said that under the blue and white flag, they cannot be relieved of their suffering but are instead oppressed by harsh taxes. Therefore, from the 16th of this month, everyone has successively suspended business to express their firm suffering. Considering that our trade association and others have always fulfilled national obligations, now that the central government has issued orders to abolish likin taxes, all industries are paying national business tax in accordance with the regulations. Only our fresh meat industry is treated as uncivilized and is still ordered to pay harsh taxes. We have no choice but to sacrifice and suspend business. We are deeply afraid that all sectors will not understand the truth, so we dare to briefly inform you. We hope that your association and all comrades will uphold justice and provide assistance. The gratitude will be boundless. With this, we wish you all peace."

The salt in this city and the surrounding areas of Su, Song, and Tai is supplied by the Liuhe salt factories. British Warship Assembled at Jiangnan Shipyard Launched the Day Before Yesterday 135

The "Da Mei Evening News" reported that the newly built British gunboat HMS Falcon, after being built and dismantled in Glasgow, England, was transported to Shanghai and entrusted to the Jiangnan Shipyard for assembly. Two Steamships Cause Disaster in the Whangpoo River 136

The Da Zhen Collides with the Gong Sheng

Due to the continuous poor weather, incidents have frequently occurred in the Whangpoo River involving merchant ships. The Da Zhen Maru, a steamship of the Shanghai-based Nisshin Kisen Kaisha, was en route from Shanghai to Hankow. While exiting Shanghai and traveling in the Whangpoo River, near the Jardine, Matheson & Co. Wharf, a British warship was anchored in the river. Fearing being hit by the strong currents, the Da Zhen Maru slowed down. At that time, the Chinese small steamship Gong Sheng was behind the Da Zhen Maru, also intending to proceed forward. Obstructed by the Da Zhen Maru, the Gong Sheng could not sail straight. Just as the Gong Sheng was trying to find a way forward, unexpectedly, the Da Zhen Maru, without regard for what was behind it, suddenly steered its ship to the left, and its hull struck the front of the Gong Sheng. The Gong Sheng was immediately damaged. Fortunately, it was 10:00 AM, and no one on board was injured. However, the damage was severe. Fortunately, the Gong Sheng was able to quickly dock, thus avoiding sinking. The Da Zhen Maru, however, was not damaged and continued on its way as usual. The Gong Sheng is currently being inspected for the extent of the damage, and repairs are being made. Meanwhile, negotiations are underway with the Japanese ship.

Japanese Ship Hits Pier

The Dai Bun Maru, a steamship of the Japanese-owned Shimomura Kisen Kaisha, arrived in Shanghai from Australia with a large shipment of wheat. After inspection at Woosung, it began sailing into the Whangpoo River at around 4:00 PM yesterday, intending to berth at Pier No. 4 to unload cargo. Unexpectedly, there were strong winds and high tides in the river at that time, and the waves were very rough. While trying to anchor, the Dai Bun Maru was pushed by the currents and lost steering control. The ship was driven by the waves to Pier No. 7 near the Jiangnan Shipyard. Its stern then violently struck the pier. The ship's propeller was damaged, and the pier was also damaged by the impact. The losses on both sides are significant. The extent of the damage is currently being assessed, and repairs will be made immediately.

The Public Announcement Committee of the Shanghai Municipal Council Was Established the Day Before Yesterday 142

Fei Er Was Elected Chairman

The newly formed Public Announcement Committee of the Municipal Council convened its establishment meeting at 3:00 PM on Monday afternoon. The following members were present: Fei Er, Ke Kesi, Ha Wo De, Tai Ke Lai, Wang Yingbin, and Watanabe. McDonald, the Chairman of the Municipal Council, delivered a speech, stating that the issue of publicizing municipal news had been discussed for a long time and had been raised repeatedly at the annual meetings of Western ratepayers. Most recently, in 1930, it was decided that the minutes of the board meetings and committee meetings, except for certain confidential matters, would be published in newspapers. However, the results of this trial implementation have not been entirely satisfactory. Therefore, this committee has been formed to discuss how to report municipal affairs to the public in a more detailed manner and to submit proposals to the board of directors. This is the responsibility of this committee. However, before you begin your deliberations, there are two points that I would like to emphasize and hope that you will keep in mind during your meetings. First, the Municipal Council's attitude that it is inconvenient for newspaper representatives to attend board meetings and committee meetings has been repeatedly approved by the annual meetings of Western ratepayers, and Mr. Fei Tang's report in the first volume also strongly supports this decision of the Municipal Council and the annual meetings of Western ratepayers. He has no intention of influencing your suggestions. The opposition to newspaper representatives attending meetings has become increasingly strong and may be generally accepted. Second, please pay special attention to the issue of publicizing municipal affairs in Chinese-language newspapers. It is fully understood that this may cause significant difficulties. However, it is hoped that the report submitted to the board of directors will have detailed discussions. Therefore, the scope of the committee's responsibilities is very broad. I dare say that improving the publicity issue is far more important for Chinese-language newspapers than for Western-language newspapers. On behalf of the board of directors, I would like to thank you for taking on this difficult task. This task has various difficulties for both newspapers and the Municipal Council. The directors and I hope that your deliberations will resolve these difficulties and satisfy ratepayers, newspapers, and the Municipal Council. Fei Er was then elected chairman of the committee, Ha Wo De was elected vice chairman, and it was agreed that meetings would be held every Monday afternoon at 3:00 PM. However, due to the holiday next Monday, the meeting will be held on Tuesday instead.

The Passenger Consistently Denies It

Pulling the Bell Is Very Important

Passengers Should Avoid Acting as Accomplices

Zhuang Linshi, a woman from Danyang, originally fell into prostitution in Nanjing. Later, Wei Dehui, the owner of a construction company, redeemed her and brought her to Shanghai to live with him. After about a year, she met Jiang Wenmei, an old acquaintance, and recounted her past. From then on, they became very close again and rekindled their old relationship. Moreover, Jiang had a large amount of money and spent it lavishly. He then had Linshi divorce Wei. The case was brought before the Special District Court, which ultimately ruled that Wei and Lin were no longer husband and wife. Wenmei then took Lin as his concubine. However, his wife at home was very strict, so Wenmei rented another house to hide her. Wenmei had a son from his original wife, who was now grown. Unexpectedly, Linshi also gave birth to a son, who was still an infant. This was discovered by the wife and her eldest son, who feared that he would grow up and share the family property. They forced Wenmei to divorce Linshi to avoid future trouble. Wenmei was naturally henpecked and gradually became distant from Linshi, but he still felt reluctant to let her go. The son that Linshi had given birth to was cared for by a wet nurse at her mother's house. Unexpectedly, the wife and her eldest son learned of this and took advantage of her absence to go to the Songshan Road police station and falsely report that there was a kidnapping ring upstairs in Zhang Lianji's building. The head of the police station sent detectives to arrest Linshi's brothers, Lin A'ao and Lin Xiaofu, and her younger sisters, Wang Yuexian and others. After questioning them, the head of the police station learned the truth and realized that it was a malicious accusation. He immediately ordered their release on bail. Tian Shugang Resolves to Walk Across the Entire Country 146

Scheduled to Depart from Shanghai on July 1st and Complete the Journey in Six Years

Using a Bicycle on Flat Ground and Carrying the Bicycle When Walking Mountain Paths

Tian Shugang, a native of Hunan, studied at the China University in Beiping for two years and is currently a professor at the Minzhi Middle School on Weihaiwei Road in Shanghai. Recently, Mr. Tian resolved to spend six years traveling around the country to collect information on customs and practices. He is scheduled to depart from Shanghai on July 1st. A reporter from the Guowen News Agency visited Mr. Tian yesterday afternoon to inquire about the purpose of his trip, the objectives of his research, and his contribution to society after completing his journey around the country. He replied as follows: "I (Tian Shugang referring to himself) am from Liling. From a young age, I had ambitions to travel far. When I was studying in Beiping, I planned to fulfill my dream of traveling around the country, but I had other commitments. I lived in Shaanxi Province for more than a year. In the past two months, I have been planning the route across the country and decided to leave Shanghai on July 1st to travel around the country by bicycle. If I encounter small paths, I will disassemble the bicycle, tie it up, and carry it on my shoulders. By the end of this year, the journey will take me through Hangzhou, Yanping, Fuzhou, Quanzhou, Xiamen, Zhangzhou, Longyan, Shanghang, Shantou, Huizhou, Guangzhou, Shaozhou, Guangzhou, Kowloon, Macau, Sanshui, Zhaoqing, Yangjiang, Leizhou, Qiongzhou, and other places. From the 21st to the 24th year of the Republic, I will go to Guizhou, Yunnan, Xikang, Tibet, Xinjiang, Mongolia, Chahar, Suiyuan, Ningxia, Gansu, Qinghai, and Sichuan. Then, in two years, I will travel through the provinces of Hubei, Hunan, Jiangxi, Anhui, Henan, Shaanxi, Shanxi, Hebei, Rehe, Heilongjiang, Jilin, Liaoning, Shandong, and Jiangsu, and then return to Shanghai. The purpose of my travels is to investigate the location, evolution, situation, geography, climate, and current status of industry and transportation in cities across the country. I will investigate the population size and culture of each place, including schools, educational institutions, industries, newspapers, libraries, museums, and other municipal constructions. In terms of scenic spots, I will examine mountains, rivers, lakes, rocks, caves, springs, sandbars, fjords, ponds, hills, tombs, pagodas, pavilions, temples, etc. I will also examine the general living conditions and customs of each place, including clothing, food, housing, and utensils. I will conduct a factual and detailed investigation, without making strange or sensational descriptions. I will write everything down in my travel notes. After completing my journey around the country, I will write a book for people to refer to and choose from. However, the four years in the middle of my journey will be more difficult. For example, when I arrive in Sichuan Province after four years, the purpose of my journey around the country will not be a problem. The difficulty of this trip lies in the Miao people of Guizhou, the Yao people of Guangxi, the Li people of Hainan Island, and the Yi people of Yunnan. I want to experience their lives firsthand and observe their lives. I will ask local Han people from each province to introduce me to the familiar Miao, Yao, Li, and Yi people, and explore their general living conditions. I will also investigate the residences and lifestyles of the wild Miao, wild Yao, wild Li, and wild Yi people in the mountains. If I can understand everything thoroughly, I will then climb the highest peak of the Himalayas, Mount Everest, and Lake Yik, which is 17,000 feet above sea level, and explore the headwaters of the Yangtze River and the Yellow River. My wish is to do what others consider difficult and unwilling to do. I am determined to create a new record!" At this point, Mr. Tian had to leave to teach a class, so the reporter said goodbye and left.

Trial Opens in the Case of the Young Owner of Hongtai Factory Being Accused of Abandonment by His Concubine 149

Huang Qingrong, the young owner of Hongtai Construction Factory on Xiaoshadu Road, lives at No. 1056 Yongtai Lane, Xinza Road. He was recently sued in the Special District Court by Huang Huangshi (32 years old), a woman from his native place, for abandonment. The lawsuit was filed by lawyer Xi Shichang. The lawsuit states that the plaintiff, Huang Huangshi, lived in the home of a Mr. Jin at No. 1074 Yongtai Lane, Xinza Road, in the spring of the 17th year of the Republic. Huang Qingrong, the landlord of the house, saw that the plaintiff was attractive and often came to flirt with her. He falsely claimed that he was not yet married and wanted to marry the plaintiff. The plaintiff believed him and was forced into an illicit relationship. About a month later, the plaintiff discovered that the defendant was already married and confronted him,责责ing him for lying and seducing women. The defendant knew he was in the wrong and expressed his apology, asking the plaintiff not to sue him. He also said that even if the plaintiff was not his wife, she could be his concubine. The plaintiff felt that what was done could not be undone, and so she let the matter drop. The defendant then gave the plaintiff 100 yuan per month for household expenses. In May of last year, she gave birth to a daughter, who was named Xiao Rong by the defendant. The living expenses were also increased from 100 yuan to 140 yuan. They lived together in this way, and their relationship was very good. The defendant's family members also came to visit from time to time, and there was never any gossip. However, in recent months, the defendant, having found another love, suddenly abandoned the plaintiff and her daughter, giving them no money and not coming home to live. When she went to him to ask for expenses, he shouted at her and refused to let her in. The plaintiff has children to raise and household affairs to take care of, and she cannot support herself. Therefore, all household expenses are dependent on the defendant. However, the defendant, having millions in assets, indulges in new loves and treats his wives and concubines like discarded shoes. He does not support his children, putting the lives of the plaintiff and her daughter in danger. Therefore, she filed a lawsuit, requesting that the defendant be punished under Article 310 of the criminal code and ordered to pay 20,000 yuan for the living expenses of the plaintiff and her daughter. According to the lawsuit, the court issued a summons and sent it to the police station to be served at the address. However, the summons was refused, and it was said that there was no such person. Therefore, when the case was heard in the Second Criminal Court by Judge Ge Zhitan yesterday afternoon, the defendant did not appear. The plaintiff, Huang Huangshi, brought her two-year-old daughter, Xiao Rong, to court and explained everything. Judge Ge ordered that the defendant be arrested and brought to court for further questioning.

Judge Guo declared that the examination confirmed that the unidentified bandit had been shot and killed while resisting arrest, and ordered that the Pushan Villa provide a coffin and burial.

The Golden Rat brand cigarettes produced by the China Tobacco Company have been widely sold. Recently, there have been profiteers who imitate and manufacture them, and have lowered their price, encroaching on the sales channels. Zhu Guisheng, an investigator of the company, investigated for a long time and finally discovered the clues. Please Thoroughly Investigate the False Accusation in the Bai Case 156

Party Headquarters' Stance

Comrade Huang Jiahui, a probationary party member of the 18th Sub-division of the Third District Party Headquarters of this city and the General Secretary of the China National Anti-Drug Association, was ordered by the Anti-Drug Association to leave Shanghai with his wife, Ms. Bai Zhiying, on March 6th to investigate the situation of smoking prohibition in Taiwan. Unexpectedly, after leaving Shanghai, his wife, Ms. Bai Zhiying, was suddenly falsely accused of trafficking morphine and was caught by the Hong Kong Customs. This was reported in newspapers for a time, causing an uproar in public opinion. The headquarters immediately sent personnel to investigate and invited Mr. Huang and his wife to the meeting for talks. It was learned that Mr. Huang has been committed to the anti-drug movement for seven years, inevitably offending various parties. Moreover, he kept the trip to Taiwan for inspection somewhat secret in advance due to the awareness of the harsh environment. Unexpectedly, this rumor arose less than ten days after leaving Shanghai. It was found that Mr. Huang went to Taiwan on March 6th, taking the Taikoo Company's Taiyuan ship from Shanghai, arriving in Xiamen on the 9th, arriving in Taiwan on the 11th, and leaving Taiwan on the 19th. The dates of arrival and departure in Taiwan are stamped on the passport by the local Keelung Police Department as proof. Therefore, from March 6th to March 19th, Mr. Huang and his wife were indeed traveling between Shanghai and Taiwan, which proves that Mr. Huang and his wife did not go to Hong Kong, so how could there be any trafficking and being caught? The certificate of proof from the Hong Kong Customs Superintendent Laut is even more powerful evidence to the contrary. The association has now found ten pieces of evidence to the contrary, which were submitted by the fifth regular meeting for resolution and presented to the Municipal Executive Committee for submission to the Central Government to thoroughly investigate the person making the false accusation. It is said that this petition was sent out yesterday.

Shen Fuchu, Li Jinsheng, Zhang Xiaoquan

The Shanghai County Public Security Bureau recently discovered that although opium, morphine, red pills, and other prohibited drugs are strictly prohibited within the county, some local traffickers are very resourceful and smuggle them into the country. Director Yan Jian, in view of this, specifically ordered all sub-bureaus to strictly arrest and detain them, especially paying attention to the stations, to ensure that drugs cannot be trafficked. After receiving the order, each sub-bureau sent police officers to search. Special Delivery

China Bank's Business Report for the 19th Year of the Republic of China (Continued) 176

The Impact of Low Silver Prices

In the Bank's report for the 18th year, it was mentioned that the lowest silver price had fallen to 21 and 5/16 pence per ounce, which was said to be the lowest record in decades. However, in the 19th year, the lowest price actually fell to 14 and a half pence. This kind of drastic and significant change has a profound impact on national finance and the social economy, which is by no means insignificant. Now, let's briefly describe its advantages and disadvantages separately. First, let's talk about its harmful effects on our country, as follows: (1) Among the foreign debts that the Chinese government has to pay, those guaranteed by customs duties are exempt from pound losses because import duties are collected in full units, which are used to pay the principal and interest of foreign debts. If silver taels are still used for calculation, this loss will be more than 30 million taels of silver compared to the previous year. As for those guaranteed by salt taxes or railway income, their income is entirely calculated in silver dollars. When converted into foreign currencies, they still have to bear the loss on exchange rates. It is estimated that the principal and interest to be paid last year for salt tax guaranteed loans, such as the British and French Hukuang and Crisp loans, totaled approximately 700,000 pounds sterling. The principal and interest to be paid last year for railway guaranteed loans, such as Beining, Zhengtai, Jinghu, and Huhang, totaled approximately 370,000 pounds sterling. The two totaled more than 1 million pounds sterling. Calculated at last year's average exchange rate of approximately 18 yuan per pound sterling, the total amount to be paid was approximately 20 million yuan, which was 7 million yuan more than the previous year's average exchange rate of approximately 11 yuan per pound sterling. Other government expenditures, such as machinery, materials, military supplies, and medicines, also had to be ordered from foreign countries at high prices due to the rise in gold prices. These are all losses suffered by public finances. (2) Since gold prices have risen, goods calculated at the original price in gold will naturally rise accordingly. Purely foreign-made products are, of course, no exception. Even domestic products whose raw materials come from overseas have to raise their selling prices to compensate. For example, canned food, cosmetics, knitwear, medicines, etc., had all increased in price by 10% by the end of last year. On the public side, the salt tax was uniformly increased by 30 cents per dan, and the price of salt rose accordingly. Railway freight rates have also been increased one after another. For example, passenger fares on the Daqing and Jiaoji Railways increased by 20%, the Xiang'e Railway by 10%, and the Pinghan, Jinpu, Pingsui, and Longhai Railways all plan to increase passenger and freight rates by 15%. The Jinghu and Huhang Railways will increase by 20%, etc., all on the grounds of coping with the rise in gold prices. All of these necessities of clothing, food, housing, and transportation have increased in price to varying degrees. Therefore, the general cost of living index in Shanghai was 107.9 in the 18th year (with 1926 as the base year), and it rose to 121.4 in the 19th year. The drastic increase can be imagined, while the increase rate of the general public's income is not enough to match it. As a result, the difficulty of the people's livelihood is even greater than before. (3) Recently, the Chinese people have been advocating domestic products and industrial construction, which are about to be carried out. However, due to the high gold prices and the rise in machinery prices, investors have generally stopped. Other public and private construction projects have also had to change or shrink their planned plans as a result. The failure to quickly rectify the railways is also partly due to this. The benefits of the fall in silver prices to China are: (1) China's total export value last year was 894,843,594 customs taels, a decrease of 120,843,724 taels compared to the 18th year, or 11.9%. The decrease in exports is a universal phenomenon in the world. The United Kingdom decreased by 21%, the United States decreased by 26.7%, and Japan decreased by 31.6%. The decrease rate of our country's exports is far smaller than the above countries, which can be said to be a blessing in disguise. If silver prices had not fallen, the decrease might have been more than this number. (2) The development of Chinese domestic industries, such as wool textiles, cotton textiles, chemicals, cosmetics, enamelware, etc., Chinese factories have increased their output and sales have increased greatly. The development situation will be discussed in another chapter. This is the most profound relationship to the country's economic future. Although the fall in silver prices has equal advantages and disadvantages for China, it has more disadvantages than advantages for the world economy. As the world economy becomes increasingly internationalized today, we should pay attention to the interests of the whole world so that world trade can restore its normal state. Therefore, the silver price problem is still an important issue in the current world economy. According to the investigation, the world's silver production last year was 243,700,000 ounces, a decrease of 17,200,000 ounces compared to the previous year. Other supply amounted to 71,500,000 ounces, an increase of 6,400,000 ounces compared to the previous year. The total supply quantity was 315,200,000 ounces, an increase of 3,700,000 ounces compared to the previous year. In terms of consumption, China used a total of 123,000,000 ounces, India used 94,500,000 ounces, other countries used 28,100,000 ounces, and arts and crafts used 35,500,000 ounces. The remaining quantity was 34,100,000 ounces, an increase of 5,200,000 ounces compared to the previous year's surplus. This is the general situation of supply and demand. In the 19th year, China's import of raw silver was 102,550,947 customs taels, and the export was 35,554,029 customs taels. The net import was 67,005,918 customs taels. If the 30,551,948 taels transported to Hong Kong are not counted as exports, the total import would be 97,557,866 customs taels. The detailed figures of imports and exports are as follows:

Location 　Import (Customs Taels) 　Export (Customs Taels)

Europe 　3,148,526 　1,043,419

Americas 　40,729,073 　256

Hong Kong and Macau 　35,464,347 　30,391,481

Saigon and Tokyo 　18,838,277 　744,915

Singapore, etc. 　756,598

Java, etc. 　58,063

India, Burma, etc. 　1,728,069 　1,772,706

Japan, Korea, and Taiwan 　2,651,655 　645,259

Philippines 　141,332

Total 　102,559,947 　35,554,029

The reason for the low silver price is not entirely due to India's sales. Although the Indian government sold 29,000,000 ounces last year, the import was 94,500,000 ounces, an increase of 20,000,000 ounces compared to the previous year. It is even less due to China's internal chaos, because China's import last year was 123,700,000 ounces, only a decrease of 13,700,000 ounces compared to the previous year. The main reason for the fall is still the general low price of goods in the world and the oversupply of silver itself. Therefore, unless the general market in the world gradually sees a turnaround or the supply of silver decreases, it is difficult for the silver price to have any hope of recovery. We dare not expect the silver price to return to its former state, but if the silver price continues to fluctuate indefinitely or even decline further, China's international trade will become increasingly depressed, and not only China will suffer. Various domestic construction plans will be difficult to carry out, and even the rectification of internal and external debts will be too burdensome to start. This has a significant relationship with all countries in the world. Therefore, the stability of the silver price is even more important than the increase in the silver price. In March of this year, the Bank's General Manager, in his personal capacity, suggested to the International Chamber of Commerce, saying that the silver price problem has reached an extremely serious area. Without the cooperation of all countries related to the silver price to study international cooperation methods, it is impossible to stabilize the silver price. It is proposed that the International Chamber of Commerce jointly propose to the International League to convene an international conference of all related countries as soon as possible to discuss this urgent issue. This proposal has been agreed by the International Chamber of Commerce and will hold a meeting in Washington in May of this year to decide to convene an international silver price conference this year. If silver producing countries and consumers cooperate with each other to help the implementation of the plan at that time, there may be a slight hope for the stability of the silver price.

Automobile News

Special Article

An Overview of the Canadian Automobile Industry 177

— Song Yu

Windsor News. The Canadian automobile industry has shown signs of revival due to the revision of automobile import tariffs. Five years ago, the Canadian automobile industry could only maintain a meager existence. This was because automobile manufacturers operated by Americans found it cheaper to set up a factory in Canada than in the Americas. Now, due to tariff protection, those who used to transport automobiles for import will inevitably manufacture them locally in order to retain the Canadian automobile market.

The reason why the Canadian automobile industry has had such a turnaround is due to Prime Minister Bennett's cabinet order to revise the automobile tariffs. As a result, automobiles from the United States are now subject to a 20% dealer discount on the local retail price. If the number exceeds 20%, it cannot be imported. This means that all automobiles worth $1,200 or more are subject to a 27% tax, and those worth less than $1,200 are subject to a 20% tax, both of which are subject to 80% of the US selling price. In the past, dealers received discounts ranging from 27% to 40%. According to importers, a 20% discount is only enough to make a living. The automobiles they sell are always relatively more expensive than automobiles of the same value manufactured in Canada.

After the promulgation of the new tariffs, automobile importers spared no effort in criticizing the Prime Minister. However, American automobile manufacturers have spent a lot of time discussing with the authorities to set up automobile manufacturing sub-factories in Canada. In the shortest time, about six or seven factories will join the Canadian industrial world. All these factories will manufacture automobiles with a selling price of about $1,000.

At present, Liwa, Heibo Mapier, and Nash have made preparations to set up factories in Canada. Liwa and Nash factories are located in Toronto, and Heibo Mapier will open a factory in Windsor. Before the cabinet order was issued, the Canadian automobile industry was organized by 11 companies and 14 factories. These companies and factories engaged in the automobile industry specialize in building and assembling trucks, buses, and passenger cars. General Motors has factories in Wahah, Windsor, and Regina. Ford factories are located everywhere, with its headquarters in Windsor. Universal Motors, Gold Fraser, General Motors, Laiham, and National Trucks are all manufactured in eastern Canada. Durant and Huila Siwa Fulan are manufactured in Toronto. The automobile industry has shown signs of decline. The sales volume of various vehicles has fallen from 30% to 27% and 20%. The import tax on parts imported into Canada is still high, so Canadian factories are likely to close. This is because the manufacturing cost of new cars is still lower than that of imported cars. Later, the government was urged by all parties to change the tax rate. For an automobile, if 50% or more of the materials used in its manufacturing are manufactured in Canada, the import tariff on parts can be reduced by 25%. However, this method still cannot allow new factories to survive, because in fact, importing is still cheaper than manufacturing locally.

The current situation has changed drastically. The value of imported automobiles is incomparable to that of those made in Canada. However, automobiles with extremely high selling prices are not included in this case, because their market sales are limited, and it is still cheaper to import them from abroad. It is expected that 500 parts manufacturers in Canada will supply the needs of new companies to manufacture automobiles. Once this is opened, the number of workers needed locally will naturally increase. In addition to the fact that one automobile can be obtained for every eight people in Canada, automobile manufacturers in the future can also export new cars to foreign countries such as British territories. All those who have special treaties with Canada can benefit from it, which is greater than exporting directly from the United States.

Canada's own automobile export industry accounts for about one-third or 50% of its production. Canada ranks third in the world in automobile production, and it is also the third largest consumer of automobiles.

Advantages and Disadvantages of Automobiles 178

— Tan Zidian

A. F. Sdgreaves, a famous Austrian automobile expert, said: Although the world's automobile production is as numerous as the sands of the Ganges and cannot be counted, the British Austin should be the first choice. The quality of an automobile depends entirely on whether the internal machinery is perfect. Austin's machinery is solid and can be called unparalleled. Moreover, it saves gasoline and has a low selling price, which is quite suitable for the middle class to buy and drive. I have been driving Austin for four years. Even in strong winds and heavy rains, I must drive on rugged mountain roads. I have not repaired it for four years. If it were not for Austin's perfect machinery and solid body, it would not have been possible.

The Ford Model A is much better than the old Ford Model T. In terms of gasoline consumption, it can save an average of two-thirds. In terms of speed, it has also made great progress.

The American Automobile Monthly once published a newspaper soliciting readers to vote for which automobile is the best in their minds. As a result, there were more than 24,000 votes.
